Using the Requests library to download the tweet image prediction (image_predictions.tsv)¶

In [3]:
url = " https://d17h27t6h515a5.cloudfront.net/topher/2017/August/599fd2ad_image-predictions/image-predictions.tsv"
response = requests.get(url)
#Saving to File
with open("image-predictions.tsv", mode="wb") as file:
    file.write(response.content)

#Creating a dataframe "df_2" using the downloaded file
df_2 = pd.read_csv("image-predictions.tsv", sep='\t')

Using the Tweepy library to query additional data via the Twitter API (tweet_json.txt)¶

Querying the Twitter API for each tweet in the Twitter archive and save JSON in a text file¶

These are hidden to comply with Twitter's API terms and conditions¶

consumer_key = 'Hidden' consumer_secret = 'Hidden' access_token = 'Hidden' access_secret = 'Hidden'

auth = OAuthHandler(consumer_key, consumer_secret) auth.set_access_token(access_token, access_secret)

api = tweepy.API(auth, wait_on_rate_limit=True)

df_1 is a DataFrame with the twitter_archive_enhanced.csv file.¶

NOTE TO REVIEWER: this student had mobile verification issues so the following¶

Twitter API code was sent to this student from a Udacity instructor¶

Tweet IDs for which to gather additional data via Twitter's API¶

tweet_ids = df_1.tweet_id.values len(tweet_ids)

Query Twitter's API for JSON data for each tweet ID in the Twitter archive¶

count = 0 fails_dict = {} start = timer()

Save each tweet's returned JSON as a new line in a .txt file¶

with open('tweet_json.txt', 'w') as outfile:

# This loop will likely take 20-30 minutes to run because of Twitter's rate limit
for tweet_id in tweet_ids:
    count += 1
    print(str(count) + ": " + str(tweet_id))
    try:
        tweet = api.get_status(tweet_id, tweet_mode='extended')
        print("Success")
        json.dump(tweet._json, outfile)
        outfile.write('\n')
    except tweepy.TweepError as e:
        print("Fail")
        fails_dict[tweet_id] = e
        pass

end = timer() print(end - start) print(fails_dict)

In [5]:
#Forming a dataframe with the "tweet_json.txt" file
with open("tweet_json.txt") as f:
    lines = f.readlines()
df_list = []
for line in lines:
    df_list.append(json.loads(line))
df_new = pd.DataFrame(df_list)
In [6]:
#Filtering the dataframe to form a dataframe with the needed columns
df_3 = df_new.filter(["id", "created_at", "favorite_count", "retweet_count"], axis=1)

OBSERVED QUALITY AND TIDINESS ISSUES WITH THE VARIOUS DATASETS¶

Quality issues¶

  1. The dataset df_1 contains retweet data in some of its columns (in_reply_to_status_id, in_reply_to_user_id, retweeted_status_id, retweeted_status_user_id, retweeted_status_timestamp, expanded_urls).

  2. Wrong datatype for the column "timestamp" in df_1 (given as "object" instead of "datetime").

  3. Wrong datatype for the column "created_at" in df_3" (given as 'object' instead of 'datetime').

  4. Date created is given as "created_as" and "timestamp" in df_3 and df_1 respectively. This is same record having different column name.

  5. The time "created_at" and "timestamp" in df_3 and df_1 respectively contains an invalid timezone.

  6. df_3 has the column "id" instead of tweet_id.

  7. df_2 column labels contains abbreviated names.

  8. The rating_numerator and rating_denominator in df_1 contains erroneous values.

Tidiness issues¶

  1. The column "tweet_id" is contained in the 3 datasets (df_1, df_2, df_3)

  2. The "timestamp"(created_at) is also contained in 2 dataframes (df_1 and df_3)

Cleaning Data¶

In [34]:
# Making copies of the original pieces of data
df1_clean = df_1.copy()
df2_clean = df_2.copy()
df3_clean = df_3.copy()

ISSUE #8¶

Define:¶

Correcting the wrong rating_numerator and rating_denominator in df1_clean. This will be done by replacing numerator outliers (ratings less than 1 and greater than 15) with the mean "rating_numerator" i.e (13), and replacing the denominator outliers ( less than or greater tan 10) with the mean rating_denominator i.e 10.

Code¶

In [53]:

In [55]:
#Replacing the numerator outlier values
for x in df1_clean.index:
    if df1_clean.loc[x, "rating_numerator"] > 15 or df1_clean.loc[x, "rating_numerator"] < 1:
        df1_clean.loc[x, "rating_numerator"] = 13
In [56]:
#Replacing the denominator outlier values
for x in df1_clean.index:
    if df1_clean.loc[x, "rating_denominator"] > 10 or df1_clean.loc[x, "rating_denominator"] < 10:
        df1_clean.loc[x, "rating_denominator"] = 10
In [57]:
#creating a column "rating" that is the division of rating_numerator by rating_denominator
df1_clean["rating"] = df1_clean["rating_numerator"] / df1_clean["rating_denominator"]

Insights:¶

  1. tweets that has the highest retweet_counts also have the highest favorite_counts(likes). This can be proven from the correlation heatmap where the correlation index between retweet_count and favorite_count is 0.93. This is a near perfect correlation and demostrates the fact that, higher favorite_counts also corresponds to a higher retweet_counts.

  2. The ratings are saturated close to the mean rating (1.06) with a standard deviation of 0.219. This shows us that the rating for each tweet are not too disperse from the other. In conclusin, most tweets are rated within a close rating margin.

  3. No "favorite_count" and "retweet_count" is independent of the dog type, as no particular dog type dominates among the highest_rated retweet and favorites.

  4. The correlation between the "rating" to the "favorite_count" and "retweet_count" is not too strong (0.38) and (0.29) respectively. This tells us that the rating given to any particular dog tweet does not directly affect the favorite and retweet counts of that tweet in a big way, rather, its a combianation of it and some other factors.
